Outline¶

Goal is to train spaCy NER from litbank data¶

✅ Load annotation data from LitBank
✅ Create train and validation sets
✅ Train NER from scratch using only language object

  • Fine-tune existing NER pipeline

  • Assess results for various approaches

  • Where do we see improvement? When is the model sufficiently useful in research?

Using spaCy version 3.2.1

from pathlib import Path
entities_path = Path.cwd() / 'litbank' / 'entities' / 'brat'

text_files = [f for f in entities_path.iterdir() if f.suffix == '.txt']
assert len(text_files) == 100
print(f'[*] imported {len(text_files)} files')

[*] imported 100 files

# for each file, create a Doc object and add the annotation data to doc.ents
# our output is a list of Doc objects 
import spacy 
from tqdm.notebook import tqdm
from spacy.tokens import Span, DocBin
from spacy.util import filter_spans


docs = []

#note: not using pretrained model because it adds predictions, just want LitBank data
nlp = spacy.blank("en")

for text_file in tqdm(text_files):
    doc = nlp(text_file.read_text())
    annotation_file = (entities_path / (text_file.stem +'.ann'))
    annotations = annotation_file.read_text().split('\n')
    ents = []
    for annotation in annotations[:-1]:
        label, start, end = annotation.split('\t')[1].split()
        span = doc.char_span(int(start), int(end), label=label)
        if span: # when start and end do not match a valid string, spaCy returns a NoneType span
            ents.append(span)
    
    filtered = filter_spans(ents)
    doc.ents = filtered
    docs.append(doc)
    

assert len(docs) == 100

# Split the data into sets for training and validation 
from sklearn.model_selection import train_test_split

train_set, validation_set = train_test_split(docs, test_size=0.2)
print(f'Created {len(train_set)} training docs')
print(f'Created {len(validation_set)} validation docs')

Created 80 training docs
Created 20 validation docs

# Add training Docs to DocBin and store to disk
from spacy.tokens import DocBin

# the DocBin will store the training documents
train_db = DocBin()
for doc in train_set:
    train_db.add(doc)
train_db.to_disk("./train.spacy")

# Save the validation Docs to disk 
validation_db = DocBin()
for doc in validation_set:
    validation_db.add(doc)
    
validation_db.to_disk("./dev.spacy") # the spaCy doc refer to development data rather than validation, change our language?

CHAPTER 1 “ Mine PER ear is open , and my heart prepared : The worst is wordly loss thou canst unfold : -- Say , is my kingdom lost ? ”
-- Shakespeare It was a feature peculiar to the colonial wars of North America LOC , that the toils and dangers of the wilderness LOC were to be encountered before the adverse hosts could meet .
A wide and apparently an impervious boundary of forests severed the possessions of the hostile provinces of France and England LOC .
The hardy colonist , and the trained European who fought at his side , frequently expended months in struggling against the rapids of the streams , or in effecting the rugged passes of the mountains PER , in quest of an opportunity to exhibit their courage in a more martial conflict .
But , emulating the patience and self-denial of the practiced native warriors PER , they learned to overcome every difficulty ; and it would seem that , in time , there was no recess of the woods LOC so dark , nor any secret place so lovely , that it might claim exemption from the inroads of those who had pledged their blood PER to satiate their vengeance , or to uphold the cold and selfish policy of the distant monarchs of Europe GPE .
Perhaps no district throughout the wide extent of the intermediate frontiers GPE can furnish a livelier picture of the cruelty and fierceness of the savage warfare of those periods than the country which lies between the head waters of the Hudson LOC and the adjacent lakes LOC .
The facilities which nature had there offered to the march of the combatants were too obvious to be neglected .
The lengthened sheet of the Champlain stretched from the frontiers of FAC Canada GPE , deep within the borders of the neighboring province of New York GPE , forming a natural passage across half the distance that the French were compelled to master PER in order to strike their enemies PER .
Near its southern termination , it received the contributions of another lake LOC , whose waters were so limpid as to have been exclusively selected by the Jesuit missionaries PER to perform the typical purification of baptism , and to obtain for it the title of lake “ du Saint Sacrement . ”
The less zealous English PER thought they conferred a sufficient honor on its unsullied fountains , when they bestowed the name of their reigning prince PER , the second of the house of Hanover .
The two PER united to rob the untutored possessors of its wooded scenery of their native right to perpetuate its original appellation of “ Horican . ”
* * As each nation of the Indians PER had its language or its dialect , they usually gave different names to the same places , though nearly all of their appellations were descriptive of the object .
Thus a literal translation of the name of this beautiful sheet of water FAC , used by the tribe that dwelt on its banks , would be “ The Tail of the Lake . ”
Lake George PER , as it is vulgarly , and now , indeed , legally , called , forms a sort of tail to Lake Champlain GPE , when viewed on the map .
Hence , the name .
Winding its way among countless islands , and imbedded in mountains , the “ holy lake ” FAC extended a dozen leagues still further to the south .
With the high plain that there interposed itself to the further passage of the water , commenced a portage of as many miles , which conducted the adventurer PER to the banks of the Hudson PER , at a point where , with the usual obstructions of the rapids PER , or rifts , as they were then termed in the language of the country LOC , the river LOC became navigable to the tide .
While , in the pursuit of their daring plans of annoyance , the restless enterprise of the French even attempted the distant and difficult gorges of the Alleghany LOC , it may easily be imagined that their proverbial acuteness PER would not overlook the natural advantages of the district GPE we have just described .
It became , emphatically , the bloody arena , in which most of the battles for the mastery of the colonies PER were contested .
Forts were erected at the different points that commanded the facilities of the route , and were taken and retaken , razed and rebuilt , as victory alighted on the hostile banners .
While the husbandman shrank back from the dangerous passes PER , within the safer boundaries of the more ancient settlements , armies larger than those that had often disposed of the scepters of the mother PER countries , were seen to bury themselves in these forests LOC , whence they rarely returned but in skeleton bands , that were haggard with care or dejected by defeat .
Though the arts of peace were unknown to this fatal region , its forests LOC were alive with men PER ; its shades and glens rang with the sounds of martial music , and the echoes of its mountains threw back the laugh , or repeated the wanton cry , of many a gallant and reckless youth , as he hurried by them , in the noontide of his spirits , to slumber in a long night of forgetfulness .
It was in this scene of strife and bloodshed that the incidents we shall attempt to relate occurred , during the third year of the war which England GPE and France GPE last waged for the possession of a country that neither was destined to retain .
The imbecility of her military leaders PER abroad , and the fatal want of energy in her councils at home FAC , had lowered the character of Great Britain from the proud elevation on which it had been placed by the talents and enterprise of her former warriors PER and statesmen PER .
No longer dreaded by her enemies PER , her servants PER were fast losing the confidence of self-respect .
In this mortifying abasement , the colonists PER , though innocent of her imbecility , and too humble to be the agents of her blunders PER , were but the natural participators .
They had recently seen a chosen army from that country PER , which , reverencing as a mother PER , they had blindly believed invincible -- an army led by ORG a chief who had been selected from a crowd of trained warriors PER , for his rare military endowments , disgracefully routed by a handful of French and Indians GPE , and only saved from annihilation by the coolness and spirit of a Virginian boy PER , whose riper fame has since diffused itself , with the steady influence of moral truth , to the uttermost confines of Christendom .
* A wide frontier had been laid naked by this unexpected disaster LOC , and more substantial evils were preceded by a thousand fanciful and imaginary dangers .
The alarmed colonists believed that the yells of the savages FAC mingled with every fitful gust of wind that issued from the interminable forests of the west LOC .
The terrific character of their merciless enemies increased immeasurably the natural horrors of warfare .
Numberless PER recent massacres were still vivid in their recollections ; nor was there any ear in the provinces so deaf as not to have drunk in with avidity the narrative of some fearful tale of midnight murder , in which the natives of the forests PER were the principal and barbarous actors PER .
As the credulous and excited traveler related the hazardous chances of the wilderness LOC , the blood of the timid curdled with terror , and mothers PER cast anxious glances even at those children PER which slumbered within the security of the largest towns .
In short , the magnifying influence of fear began to set at naught the calculations of reason , and to render those who should have remembered their manhood PER , the slaves of the basest passions PER .
Even the most confident and the stoutest hearts began to think the issue of the contest was becoming doubtful ; and that abject class was hourly increasing in numbers , who thought they foresaw all the possessions of the English crown in America subdued by their Christian foes , or laid waste by the inroads of their relentless allies .
* Washington PER , who , after uselessly admonishing the European general of the danger into which he was heedlessly running PER , saved the remnants of the British army ORG , on this occasion , by his decision and courage .
The reputation earned by Washington PER in this battle was the principal cause of his being selected to command the American armies at a later day .
It is a circumstance worthy of observation , that while all America PER rang with his well-merited reputation PER , his name does not occur in any European account of the battle ; at least the author PER has searched for it without success .
In this manner does the mother PER country absorb even the fame , under that system of rule .
When , therefore , intelligence was received at the fort which covered the southern termination of the portage between the Hudson and the FAC lakes , that Montcalm PER had been seen moving up the Champlain , with an army ORG “ numerous as the leaves on the trees , ” its truth was admitted with more of the craven LOC reluctance of fear than with the stern joy that a warrior should feel , in finding an enemy PER within reach of his blow .
The news had been brought , toward the decline of a day in midsummer , by an Indian runner PER , who also bore an urgent request from Munro PER , the commander of a work on the shore of the “ holy lake , ” PER for a speedy and powerful reinforcement .
It has already been mentioned that the distance between these two posts PER was less than five leagues PER .
The rude path , which originally formed their line of communication , had been widened for the passage of wagons FAC ; so that the distance which had been traveled by the son of the forest in two hours PER , might easily be effected by a detachment of troops , with their necessary baggage PER , between the rising and setting of a summer sun .
The loyal servants of the British crown had given to one of these forest-fastnesses PER the name of William Henry PER , and to the other that of Fort Edward PER , calling each after a favorite prince of the reigning family PER .
The veteran Scotchman just named held the first , with a regiment of regulars and a few provincials PER ; a force really by far too small to make head against the formidable power that Montcalm PER was leading to the foot of his earthen mounds .
At the latter , however , lay General Webb , who commanded the armies of the king in the northern provinces PER , with a body of more than five thousand men PER .
By uniting the several detachments of his command , this officer PER might have arrayed nearly double that number of combatants against the enterprising Frenchman PER , who had ventured so far from his reinforcements , with an army but little superior in numbers .
But under the influence of their degraded fortunes , both officers PER and men PER appeared better disposed to await the approach of their formidable antagonists , within their works , than to resist the progress of their march , by emulating the successful example of the French at Fort du Quesne GPE , and striking a blow on their advance .
After the first surprise of the intelligence had a little abated , a rumor was spread through the entrenched camp FAC , which stretched along the margin of the Hudson , forming a chain of outworks to the body of the fort itself , that a chosen detachment of fifteen hundred men PER was to depart , with the dawn , for William Henry PER , the post at the northern extremity of the portage FAC .
That which at first was only rumor , soon became certainty , as orders passed from the quarters of the commander-in-chief PER to the several corps he had selected for this service , to prepare for their speedy departure .
All doubts as to the intention of Webb now vanished , and an hour or two of hurried footsteps and anxious faces succeeded .
The novice in the military art flew from point to point , retarding his own preparations by the excess of his violent and somewhat distempered zeal ; while the more practiced veteran PER made his arrangements with a deliberation that scorned every appearance of haste ; though his sober lineaments and anxious eye sufficiently betrayed that he had no very strong professional relish for the , as yet , untried and dreaded warfare of the wilderness LOC .
At length the sun set in a flood of glory , behind the distant western hills FAC , and as darkness drew its veil around the secluded spot the sounds of preparation diminished ; the last light finally disappeared from the log cabin of some officer PER ; the trees cast their deeper shadows over the mounds and the rippling stream , and a silence soon pervaded the camp FAC , as deep as that which reigned in the vast forest by which it was environed LOC .

CHAPTER 1 “ Mine ear is open , and my heart prepared : The worst is wordly loss thou canst unfold : -- Say , is my kingdom FAC lost ? ”
-- Shakespeare PER It was a feature peculiar to the colonial wars of North America GPE , that the toils and dangers of the wilderness LOC were to be encountered before the adverse hosts PER could meet .
A wide and apparently an impervious boundary of forests LOC severed the possessions of the hostile provinces of France and England GPE .
The hardy colonist PER , and the trained European who fought at his side PER , frequently expended months in struggling against the rapids of the streams LOC , or in effecting the rugged passes of the mountains LOC , in quest of an opportunity to exhibit their courage in a more martial conflict .
But , emulating the patience and self-denial of the practiced native warriors PER , they learned to overcome every difficulty ; and it would seem that , in time , there was no recess of the woods LOC so dark , nor any secret place so lovely , that it might claim exemption from the inroads of those who had pledged their blood to satiate their vengeance , or to uphold the cold and selfish policy of the distant monarchs of Europe PER .
Perhaps no district throughout the wide extent of the intermediate frontiers LOC can furnish a livelier picture of the cruelty and fierceness of the savage warfare of those periods than the country which lies between the head waters of the Hudson and the adjacent lakes LOC .
The facilities which nature PER had there LOC offered to the march of the combatants PER were too obvious to be neglected .
The lengthened sheet of the Champlain LOC stretched from the frontiers of Canada GPE , deep within the borders of the neighboring province of New York LOC , forming a natural passage across half the distance that the French were compelled to master in order to strike their enemies LOC .
Near its southern termination PER , it received the contributions of another lake , whose waters were so limpid as to have been exclusively selected by the Jesuit missionaries to perform the typical purification of baptism , and to obtain for it the title of lake “ du Saint Sacrement . ” LOC
The less zealous English PER thought they conferred a sufficient honor on its unsullied fountains LOC , when they bestowed the name of their reigning prince PER , the second of the house of Hanover PER .
The two GPE united to rob the untutored possessors of its wooded scenery PER of their native right to perpetuate its original appellation of “ Horican LOC . ”
* * As each nation of the Indians GPE had its language or its dialect , they usually gave different names to the same places LOC , though nearly all of their appellations were descriptive of the object .
Thus a literal translation of the name of this beautiful sheet of water LOC , used by the tribe that dwelt on its banks GPE , would be “ The Tail of the Lake LOC . ”
Lake George LOC , as it is vulgarly , and now , indeed , legally , called , forms a sort of tail to Lake Champlain LOC , when viewed on the map .
Hence , the name .
Winding its way among countless islands LOC , and imbedded in mountains LOC , the “ holy lake LOC ” extended a dozen leagues still further to the south .
With the high plain that there interposed itself to the further passage of the water LOC , commenced a portage of as many miles , which conducted the adventurer to the banks of the Hudson , at a point where , with the usual obstructions of the rapids , or rifts , as they were then termed in the language of the country , the river became navigable to the tide LOC .
While , in the pursuit of their daring plans of annoyance , the restless enterprise of the French GPE even attempted the distant and difficult gorges of the Alleghany LOC , it may easily be imagined that their proverbial acuteness would not overlook the natural advantages of the district we have just described LOC .
It became , emphatically , the bloody arena , in which most of the battles for the mastery of the colonies were contested LOC .
Forts FAC were erected at the different points that commanded the facilities of the route LOC , and were taken and retaken , razed and rebuilt , as victory alighted on the hostile banners .
While the husbandman PER shrank back from the dangerous passes LOC , within the safer boundaries of the more ancient settlements LOC , armies larger than those that had often disposed of the scepters of the mother countries ORG , were seen to bury themselves in these forests , whence they rarely returned but in skeleton bands , that were haggard with care or dejected by defeat LOC .
Though the arts of peace were unknown to this fatal region LOC , its forests LOC were alive with men PER ; its shades and glens rang with the sounds of martial music , and the echoes of its mountains LOC threw back the laugh , or repeated the wanton cry , of many a gallant and reckless youth PER , as he hurried by them , in the noontide of his spirits , to slumber in a long night of forgetfulness .
It was in this scene of strife and bloodshed that the incidents we shall attempt to relate occurred , during the third year of the war which England GPE and France GPE last waged for the possession of a country that neither was destined to retain LOC .
The imbecility of her military leaders abroad PER , and the fatal want of energy in her councils at home PER , had lowered the character of Great Britain GPE from the proud elevation on which it had been placed by the talents and enterprise of her former warriors PER and statesmen PER .
No longer dreaded by her enemies PER , her servants PER were fast losing the confidence of self-respect .
In this mortifying abasement , the colonists PER , though innocent of her imbecility , and too humble to be the agents of her blunders , were but the natural participators PER .
They had recently seen a chosen army from that country , which , reverencing as a mother , they had blindly believed invincible ORG -- an army led by a chief who had been selected from a crowd of trained warriors , for his rare military endowments , disgracefully routed by a handful of French and Indians , and only saved from annihilation by the coolness and spirit of a Virginian boy , whose riper fame has since diffused itself , with the steady influence of moral truth , to the uttermost confines of Christendom ORG .
* A wide frontier LOC had been laid naked by this unexpected disaster , and more substantial evils were preceded by a thousand fanciful and imaginary dangers .
The alarmed colonists PER believed that the yells of the savages PER mingled with every fitful gust of wind that issued from the interminable forests of the west LOC .
The terrific character of their merciless enemies PER increased immeasurably the natural horrors of warfare .
Numberless recent massacres were still vivid in their recollections ; nor was there any ear in the provinces so deaf as not to have drunk in with avidity the narrative of some fearful tale of midnight murder , in which the natives of the forests PER were the principal and barbarous actors LOC .
As the credulous and excited traveler PER related the hazardous chances of the wilderness LOC , the blood of the timid PER curdled with terror , and mothers PER cast anxious glances even at those children which slumbered within the security of the largest towns PER .
In short , the magnifying influence of fear began to set at naught the calculations of reason , and to render those who should have remembered their manhood , the slaves of the basest passions PER .
Even the most confident and the stoutest hearts began to think the issue of the contest was becoming doubtful ; and that abject class PER was hourly increasing in numbers , who thought they foresaw all the possessions of the English crown GPE in America GPE subdued by their Christian foes PER , or laid waste by the inroads of their relentless allies PER .
* Washington PER , who , after uselessly admonishing the European general PER of the danger into which he was heedlessly running , saved the remnants of the British army ORG , on this occasion , by his decision and courage .
The reputation earned by Washington PER in this battle was the principal cause of his being selected to command the American armies ORG at a later day .
It is a circumstance worthy of observation , that while all America GPE rang with his well-merited reputation , his name does not occur in any European GPE account of the battle ; at least the author PER has searched for it without success .
In this manner does the mother country GPE absorb even the fame , under that system of rule .
When , therefore , intelligence was received at the fort which covered the southern termination of the portage between the Hudson and the lakes FAC , that Montcalm PER had been seen moving up the Champlain LOC , with an army “ numerous as the leaves on the trees , ” ORG its truth was admitted with more of the craven reluctance of fear than with the stern joy that a warrior PER should feel , in finding an enemy within reach of his blow PER .
The news had been brought , toward the decline of a day in midsummer , by an Indian runner , who also bore an urgent request from Munro , the commander of a work on the shore of the “ holy lake , ” for a speedy and powerful reinforcement PER .
It has already been mentioned that the distance between these two posts FAC was less than five leagues .
The rude path FAC , which originally formed their line of communication , had been widened for the passage of wagons ; so that the distance which had been traveled by the son of the forest PER in two hours , might easily be effected by a detachment of troops , with their necessary baggage PER , between the rising and setting of a summer sun .
The loyal servants of the British crown PER had given to one of these forest-fastnesses FAC the name of William Henry FAC , and to the other that of Fort Edward FAC , calling each after a favorite prince of the reigning family PER .
The veteran Scotchman just named PER held the first , with a regiment of regulars ORG and a few provincials PER ; a force really by far too small to make head against the formidable power that Montcalm was leading to the foot of his earthen mounds ORG .
At the latter , however , lay General Webb , who commanded the armies of the king in the northern provinces PER , with a body of more than five thousand men PER .
By uniting the several detachments of his command ORG , this officer PER might have arrayed nearly double that number of combatants PER against the enterprising Frenchman , who had ventured so far from his reinforcements , with an army but little superior in numbers PER .
But under the influence of their degraded fortunes , both officers PER and men PER appeared better disposed to await the approach of their formidable antagonists PER , within their works , than to resist the progress of their march , by emulating the successful example of the French GPE at Fort du Quesne GPE , and striking a blow on their advance .
After the first surprise of the intelligence had a little abated , a rumor was spread through the entrenched camp , which stretched along the margin of the Hudson , forming a chain of outworks to the body of the fort itself FAC , that a chosen detachment of fifteen hundred men was to depart , with the dawn , for William Henry , the post at the northern extremity of the portage ORG .
That which at first was only rumor , soon became certainty , as orders passed from the quarters of the commander-in-chief FAC to the several corps he had selected for this service ORG , to prepare for their speedy departure .
All doubts as to the intention of Webb PER now vanished , and an hour or two of hurried footsteps and anxious faces succeeded .
The novice in the military art PER flew from point to point , retarding his own preparations by the excess of his violent and somewhat distempered zeal ; while the more practiced veteran PER made his arrangements with a deliberation that scorned every appearance of haste ; though his sober lineaments and anxious eye sufficiently betrayed that he had no very strong professional relish for the , as yet , untried and dreaded warfare of the wilderness LOC .
At length the sun set in a flood of glory , behind the distant western hills LOC , and as darkness drew its veil around the secluded spot LOC the sounds of preparation diminished ; the last light finally disappeared from the log cabin of some officer FAC ; the trees cast their deeper shadows over the mounds and the rippling stream , and a silence soon pervaded the camp FAC , as deep as that which reigned in the vast forest LOC by which it was environed .
